<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Excludes Volvo, Jaguar and Land Rover sales. Also excludes heavy trucks.  </p>

<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">UPDATE 1-Online retailers winners in UK Christmas trading  </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>BY</b> </td><td>By Rachel Sanderson  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>539 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>3 January 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>18:50</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">(Recasts lead, adds background in paragraph 10)  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">LONDON, Jan 3 (Reuters) - Online retailers look set to be crowned among the victors of Britain's Christmas trading war this year alongside an uneven showing on the high street.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Internet sales in Britain for the first time peaked during the start of seasonal discounting last week after surging more than 50 percent in the run up to Christmas, online retail tracker IMRG reported.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">It was the opposite story for Britain's high street with the number of Britons visiting stores down 6.8 percent in the week after Christmas, according to data from FootFall on Wednesday.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"This has definitely been an online Christmas," James Roper, chief executive of the Interactive Media in Retail Group (IMRG) said. "We think 25 million people now shop on the Internet."  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Roper said early evidence showed online Christmas sales are looking to be around half a billion pounds better than already strong industry forecasts, and will top 7.5 billion pounds ($15 billion) in the 10 weeks leading up to the holiday.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">More surprisingly, Roper said data from IMRG and eDigital Research showed that unlike in previous years, there was no sign of a post-Christmas fall in online demand.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Instead, visits to the online stores of leading British retailers on Dec. 27 -- the start of the holiday discounting season -- spiked 30 percent higher than any previous peak.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"The young Internet shopping industry is already a huge success, with potential to continue to grow at 40 percent per annum for the foreseeable future," Roper said.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">INTERNET ADVANTAGE  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Early reports suggest British retailers made an uneven showing during crucial Christmas trading while many consumers struggled with soaring household bills, higher borrowing costs and tame wage growth.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Premium grocers, luxury goods stores as well as Britain's biggest retailer Tesco are expected to have performed strongly while middle market store owners have struggled.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">However, there are indications a strong Internet strategy will have helped to separate winners from the losers.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Tesco, the world's fifth largest retailer, which forecast a "good Christmas," saw visitors to Tesco.com swell to 1.3 million over the holiday period. PC World and Curry's are expected to benefit from parent company DSG International's early push into online selling.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Analysts predict the Christmas fortunes of clothing retailer Next , which reports on Thursday, rest on the success of its home and online shopping Directory business.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"Part of the reason why high street retailers are having a tough time is due to the inexorable rise of home shopping via the Internet," Investec Securities analyst Mark Charnock wrote in a note last month.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Among those hardest hit are some middle market retailers and sellers of music and movies who are suffering from a boom in downloads from the likes of Apple's iTunes.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Woolworths and HMV issued profit warnings before Christmas while Music Zone, a privately-owned DVD and CD store, filed for administration on Wednesday.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Data from Internet tracker Hitwise showed visits to music download sites rose 50 percent from Christmas Day 2005.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />BRITAIN-CHRISTMAS/INTERNET (UPDATE 1)|LANGEN|ABN|E|RBN|U|UKI|BNX|RNP|DNP|PCO</td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>IN</b> </td><td><br />i64 : Retail/Wholesale | iint : Internet/Online Services | ilea : Leisure/Arts</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>NS</b> </td><td><br />e11 : Economic Performance/Indicators | glife : Living/Lifestyle | mcat : Commodity/Financial Market News | ecat : Economic News | gcat : Political/General News | ncat : Content Types | nfact : Factiva Filters | nfce : FC&amp;E Exclusion Filter</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RE</b> </td><td><br />eurz : Europe | uk : United Kingdom | weurz : Western Europe | eecz : European Union Countries</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>IPC</b> </td><td><br />RET | WWW | CPX | LIF | LEI | WIN | ECI | MCE</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>PUB</b> </td><td><br />Reuters Limited</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>AN</b> </td><td><br />Document LBA0000020070103e3130016b</td></tr></tbody></table><br /></div>

<table cellspacing="1" cellpadding="1" border="0"><tbody><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>HD</b> </td><td><b class="enHeadline">RPT-UK shopper numbers fall 6.8 pct post-Xmas yr/yr  </b>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>WC</b> </td><td>289 words</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>PD</b> </td><td>3 January 2007</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>ET</b> </td><td>15:22</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SN</b> </td><td><a onclick="var RIND=window.RIND||window.parent.RIND;RIND.getEntityDetails('','LBA','sc','False', '');return false;;return false;" href="javascript:void(0)">Reuters News</a></td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>SC</b> </td><td>LBA</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>LA</b> </td><td>English</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><b>CY</b> </td><td>(c) 2007 Reuters Limited  </td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>LP</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">(repeats to additional subscribers with no changes to text) LONDON, Jan 3 (Reuters) - British shoppers heading into the stores fell 6.8 percent in the week after Christmas compared with a year ago, retail tracker FootFall said on Wednesday.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">It is a sharp fall-off from the start of the week, when footfall rose 6.9 percent on Boxing Day compared with a year ago as shoppers surged into stores for the beginning of the discounting season.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><p><b>TD</b> </p></td><td><p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">FootFall Marketing Manager Natasha Burton cautioned that the figures did not provide a complete picture of Christmas shopping, particularly as it omitted online sales. The fall was also slightly less than in the week before Christmas when footfall in stores was down around 8 percent.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">"This is purely footfall to bricks and mortar stores, it doesn't include other channels, like the Internet," Burton told Reuters by telephone.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Economists have warned they do not expect a blockbuster performance from the high street while many consumers continued to struggle with soaring household bills, higher borrowing costs and tame wage growth.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">However, there are indications a strong Internet strategy is likely to have helped separate the winners from the losers.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">James Roper, chief executive of London-based online tracker Interactive Media in Retail Group (IMRG) said on Wednesday, anecdotal evidence suggested online sales surged more than 50 percent to 7.5 billion pounds ($14.8 billion), much higher than anticipated, in the 10 weeks running up to Christmas.  </p>
<p class="articleParagraph enarticleParagraph">Roper, in a telephone interview, said he expected to release firm data on Internet sales later this month.  </p>
</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RF</b> </td><td><br />BRITAIN-CHRISTMAS/FOOTFALL (REFILE)|LANGEN|ABN|E|RBN|UKI|D|M|RNP|DNP</td></tr>
<tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>IN</b> </td><td><br />i64 : Retail/Wholesale | iint : Internet/Online Services</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>NS</b> </td><td><br />e11 : Economic Performance/Indicators | mcat : Commodity/Financial Market News | ecat : Economic News | ncat : Content Types | nfact : Factiva Filters | nfce : FC&amp;E Exclusion Filter</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>RE</b> </td><td><br />eurz : Europe | uk : United Kingdom | weurz : Western Europe | eecz : European Union Countries</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>IPC</b> </td><td><br />RET | MCE | ECI | WWW</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>PUB</b> </td><td><br />Reuters Limited</td></tr><tr><td valign="top" align="right" class="index"><br /><b>AN</b> </td><td><br />Document LBA0000020070103e313000td</td></tr></tbody></table><br /></div>
